# Parliament of the Snake — Edited Manuscript

---

PART ONE  ACT 1: THE EGGMAN    1  ACT ONE The Eggman Night fell on Residential Zone 42 Designation Cloudtop View. Not to worry, nothing damaged, just its pride. A time bitten building squats deep at the heart of the Zone, all boarded up windows and crumbling brick, long broken doors still claiming to be automatic, the hastily patched holes in the roof a monument to local governance and budget realities. In the shadowy depths of the hall a weekly ritual takes place. Hooded figures murmur in hushed tones, a muted babble of incantation burbling as the undertones of a stream. A sacred tome is passed between them, each figure hastily scrawling their rune on its pages. A sharp hiss comes from the midst of the disciples, silence, followed by mutters resuming with renewed vigour, a swelling, rushing cadence rising and rising into a point, into a cacophony, a torrent of voices converging as one until a single, booming voice-  “Right,right have we all signed it then? ”  The register is hastily passed to the late comers and dawdlers.

---

Hoods are lowered-  “Pissing it down out there. ”  “Stick the light on Naj. ”  Chairs are dragged from the back of the hall, instant coffees are poured from those massive water urns you only ever see on knackered school tables, phones are put away and a ring of seats is created so that each member might get a full view of the face of their cohorts. “Hill Top Neighbourhood Watch Session Eighty Four is now in...session ”  Biscuits are dunked, coughs are coughed, little waves to say hello are waved hello and a mewling goat is sacrificed to the great lord Apothis, its blood spilt with a bejewelled dagger of H 'gok, the crimson ichor adding to the decades of stains encrusted upon the lino of the meeting hall. “Julie, are you alright taking the minutes again my love? ”  One of those other things didn't happen*   The goat HAD been talked about at Hill Top Neighbourhood Watch Full Session Eight but at it had been agreed that it wasn 't really fair to expect Sally to clean that up before Fighting the Fat for the Over Fifties  “You can count on me Roger ” Julie flourished her Very Expensive Pen at the rest of the group, her oversize notepad already resting in the crook of her arm.

---

“Very, very good ” Roger Harvey, Special Zonal Constable and imposing moustache haver settled down into his chair, the best chair, the one in the hall that had some memories of what it was like to have a cushion. He was the leader of this group of vigilant citizens, the poobah, the big cheese. The Foreman. He pored over the register. “Shirley yes there we are, Hannah have we got Hannah? ”  “Just coming Roger ” Hannah Wrigley did that sort of running but not running run over to her chair, ably flinging a tea bag into the bin as she passed. Noses wrinkled. “Sorry all, its my special tea, its good for gut health ” A waft of ginseng and beef washed over the coven. She adjusted her dungarees and beamed at the rest of the group “It does wonders for my regularity. ”  Roger twitched his moustache and continued reading. It was a moustaches that only important men could grow, corporals, captains, heads of finance from the 1950s. “First and foremost, Daz provides his apologises, he has been brung low by his bowels ” he worked his jowls all the way around the word bowels . “Oop someones infested ” said Shirley. “I am assured he is not. Who, who is present? I have Naj, Paul Bond. Esmerelda?

---

Have we got Esmerelda? ”  A figure lurking by the door took a last longing drag of her cigarette and threw the butt out into the rain, dragging the door shut behind her. She shook off a knitted raspberry beret, bottle dyed black hair dropping to just above her shoulders, flecks of grey sparkling along the tips. She jangled as she moved, her arms covered in enough metal to make her at least partly magnetic. Her eyes were a deep brown set into a sharp, high cheekboned like an elf but a Lord of the Rings one not a Christmas one. Less mystical, just a bit foresty, she wore heavy black boots and loose denim jeans, Ride the Lightning emblazoned on her black vest. “Yeah I 'm here ” her voice was deep and welsh, it cracked at the end “Can we stick to Jones Rog? Pretty please? ”  “Good, good to see you Esmerelda ” he shuffled both his papers and his moustache officiously “Before we carry on I must check, must confirm why you missed Session 83? No apologies were provided for your absence. ”  “Eh? ”  Moustache twitching, he tapped the page with his Less Expensive But Still Quite Nice Pen “Last week Esmerelda, you missed last week.

---

There were no apologies provided. ” Sometimes it felt like the moustache was talking to you, but that was bollocks, because it was a moustache and moustaches can 't talk. Yet. “I told you I couldn 't gonna make it ” she could 've made it “I told you at Emergency Session whatever it was. ”  “Point of Order ” Shirleys voice was that of a stood on vole, her face was too, she crooked one bony finger to the sky “Did you put it in the Govchat? ” Shirley, the living embodiment of her leopard print pant suit. Hard to look at and generally offensive. “No, I didn't put it in the Govchat ” Jones glared “I couldn 't message all day. Comms privileges gone. Forgot to take a book back to the library ” she stuck her tongue out at Shirley. Library book, drunk in public at eleven in the morning, it was all the same. “If you 're going to miss the meeting you put it in the chat, even if you are the local malcontent ” the expression that moved across Shirleys face was usually reserved for an especially misplaced shit. Charming.

---

“They 're the rules Esmerelda, if you 're going to, going to miss- ”  “-the meeting put it in the Govchat yes but I literally saw you the night before, I was there, in your living room, telling you I wasn 't coming. ”  “Its about rules Esmerelda, just about rules. Where would we be if the rules weren 't kept to and people just did what they want ” he actually harrumphed, the mustachioed elephant git actually harrumphed. “I love it when you say that Roger ” Julie glowed at him. “Yes, well, yes, lets, erm ” he went a little bit redder than usual and cleared his throat. “I 'll mark it as a miss but if there is a recurrence, a repeat, then I 'm afraid, as per, as per the protocol we 'll have to discuss your adherence to your community order. An appointed official such as myself can 't be seen to be covering for your continued societal disorder. ”  Jones ' eyes rolled so far back in her head that she could briefly see her past. That was the thing with community service, it didn 't sound so bad at the time. “Yes sir Roger sir ” she ripped a commendably accurate salute.

---

“Okay now that thats sorted ” Roger cleared his throat, lungs and part of his pancreas “Onto Business. ”   He flourished the agenda as he rose “I shall commence, as ever ” twitch of the moustache “with the reading of the Agenda. Agenda Item Number One, Residential Zone 42 Designation Cloudtop View Updates, Item Number Two, Talking, Talking Points, Agenda Item Number, Number Three, Any other business. ”  The group nodded sagely, as much as a group of people is able to nod in such co-ordination that you can call a group movement sage. Roger stoically kept the agenda to three items, numbers above three were the province of inefficiency. It was a godsend if you, like Jones, spent the majority of the meetings thinking about venus fly traps, or capuchin monkeys with top hats, or both. “For Item number one I 'm going to- ”  “Sorry Rog can I just say something I 'm going to have to make a Point of Order ” Paul Bond leapt to his feet, an uncoiling wanker of a spring, big teeth he couldn 't talk around and floppy brown hair you could surgically remove from his head and turn into a really good wig.

---

This was Paul Bonds tenth meeting, he 'd replaced Eddie Trulove after he got kicked out for accidentally flashing his willy to a street sprayer. The third of Paul Bonds meetings had ended with him giving Roger a rundown on how Agendas should really be written. At his fourth meeting he 'd offered to take over as chair, then called for an unsuccessful vote of no confidence in Roger by his sixth. Roger thought Paul Bond was still plotting. Jones thought he was a wriggly little bell end. “I was running through the rules as some light bed time reading ” he flapped a stack of papers “It says here thank you very much,Rule 17a the newest member of the Neighbourhood Watch is to bring the first talking point to the group, have you forgotten? I hope you haven 't forgotten. ”  “No, no, not forgotten no I was just coming to you Paul, go ahead Paul ” plotter or not you wouldn 't catch Roger not going by the rules. “Cheers Rog ” Paul Bond opened his arms with an obsequious smile “Nothing from me thank you. ”  “Excellent cheers Paul Bond, always happy for you to have your moment ” Jones tutted at him.

---

“Just following protocol Jones where would we- ”  “Thank you both ” Roger produced a notepad from the recesses of his deep overcoat pockets and flipped to a page very clearly marked SESSION 84 “The first talking point for review was the recent spate of Unauthorised Gatherings we 've been seeing recently, I know its been a big concern in the Cloudtop General Chat and- ”  Sometimes she thought it 'd be better to just do the time. Stop turning up, let Roger shop her in. He 'd like that, he loved doing official stuff. “-don 't believe theres the appetite to report in the wider neighbourhood so it falls to us, the Watch- ”  Maybe he wouldn 't. He was alright was Roger. She got mugged once. It wasn 't that bad like, just some Tweener followed her up the hill with a knife, wasting his time unless he was desperate for a lighter and three quid. Still, it was Roger whos curtains twitched the fastest, he was straight out of his house chasing the kid off bad knee and all. Her knight in battered armour. The estates curtains had never been twitchier after that, they even had two drones for a bit.

---

Julie was spotted wandering the streets with a baseball bat, until the police found out, thank you very much Mrs Cooper but we 'll have none of your vigilante justice thank you very much. “Now I 've had a word with the Constabulary and they have informed me the Drone hasn 't reported back anything out of the ordinary, nothing out of it, in fact theres been a drop in- ”  Jones could just not turn up, but then the moustache would be sad, and she liked the moustache, even if it was stealing hours of her life. “-Sally Bindis knickers- ”  They might be the type of people to report teenagers to the order police for having a late night snog, or the type of people to listen at your door for any music produced post 2001, but they were her people. And it was this or lose all her Friendship Permits. Or go to prison. And she didn 't want to go to prison. Not nowadays. “If anything, If anything I 'd love to give them some tips on how to cook so there isn 't so much, so much smoke. ”  “Ah, ah, Rog, time ” Naj Goldblum tapped laconically at a thick gold watch on his arm.

---

Naj was a bloke who 'd got it right, turn up for your free coffee, tap your watch every ten minutes and lay about like you 're being fed grapes you beautiful, chest forested man you. “Thats all, thats all for Constabulary Updates. Commencing, commencing Agenda Item number two. I 'm going to pass over to Julie- ”  “Oh for christs sake three weeks in a row ” Shirley groaned. “-to Julie ” Roger growled “whos raised a, raised a concern this week ” if a moustache was capable of passing over the baton of conversation to another human being that is exactly what would have happened here. It isn 't, but you try and imagine it doing it.

---

Julie stood brandishing a finger “Something must be do- ”  “Excuse me ” Paul Bond boinged back to his feet, Julies finger remained amidst brandish, her mouth open “If Julies speaking whos taking the minutes? ” he gnawed at one knuckle “I can 't be part of a meeting where minutes don 't get minuted. ”  “Good point Paul Bond good point ” Roger raised a hand in placation “Esmerelda, would you take the opportunity to get back into our good books and take the, take the minutes for us whilst Julies speaking. ”  Jones jolted from a reverie centered around what she was going to have for dinner tonight and how much of it was going to be made of wine. “Do the wha? ”  All of it. It was all of her dinner. “The minutes. ”  “The minutes? ” she shrugged an apology “To be completely honest Roger I 'll most likely stop listening and just draw a cock and bollocks so you 're best off passing it to someone else ”  Rogers smile froze in place, a complex arithmetic began in his head. “Well at least shes honest ” Shirley snatched the clipboard and Very Expensive Pen from Julies reluctant, unbrandished hand “Dont worry I 'll be gentle with it ” she cackled.

---

“A cock ” Rogers eyes were glazed over with a confused mist. “Are you OK Roger really Esmerelda that was very rude ” Julie put a hand gently on his arm. “Oh come on Rog can we just get on with it ” Jones did her best to at least look a little contrite. “And bollocks. ”   “Sorry to be a pain Roger ” Hannah squeaked “ but can we please just, maybe, get on with this a little bit? I 've left a Limburger Zucchini baking in the oven and I really wouldn 't want to have to pick off the burnt bits. ”  “Ah, ah I 'd kindve like to agree ” Naj, prostrate across two chairs flicked a curl of dark hair from across his amber eyes. Rogers eyes cleared, his moustache twitching off the debris of a potential mental breakdown. “Yes, sorry, yes, sorry, Item on erm, item on the agenda would be … ” he waved Julie on, mouthing bollocks to himself. “Thank you Roger.

---

Something must be done! ” she rebrandished the finger “Three days until the switch on ad I can already feel the migraines coming. ”  “I take it, shall take it that you 're talking, once more, about the ” Roger furrowed his brow and checked his notepad “impending death waves coming from the top of Simcock Hill. ”  “The very same Roger ” Julie loved a good furrowed brow the minx you could see it on her face “I 've been reading up on it every evening this week and I 'm absolutely positive theres ” she paused for effect “ something dodgy about it. ”  “ This would be the Harmony, Harmony mast, the same ones that have been installed in half of the, half of the Residential Zones in the country. ”  “Pfaah ” she pfaahed “Harmony my foot, they 're dangerous, them signals messing with your brain chemistry, they cause cancer, exploding heads, all sorts I 've heard. One man in Zone 18 cooked a rotisserie chicken under one. ”  “You need to stay off dodgy Govchats ” said Shirley.

---

“Actually Julie thank you very much the Oohashi nodes have been shown to cause a sixteen percent drop in crime and thiry six percent of residents reported a new found sensation of peace and tranquility ” Paul Bond peered down from his high horse “Frequency programming was instrumental in the eradication of the Pulpos, its all very tested, very safe. I spent time as a hypersonic researcher, these baseless conspiracy theories are a bit sad when you know how this tech works. Its programming people to be peaceful. ”  “And how manys faces bubbled off? ” Julie turned the finger on him “Your analysing tell you that? How can we trust something used to explodes Octopuses? ”  “Julie, Julie, you really must, must trust the government in this. Its a completely different frequency, the frequency, frequency of the future. Programming the present. ”  “Pfah. Trust the snake? Vetko Block wouldn 't have stood for this you mark my words. ”  “Probably would have had you killed for questioning it though ” Jones counted herself amongst the fortunate to have only experienced the former Prime Ministers special brand of justice second hand. “At least you knew where you stood ” Julies shoulders slumped as she sat back in her chair “I can 't sleep Roger.

---

I can feel it in my head. Vibrating all the time, its right on top of my house. Workmen coming and going at all hours, banging about doing who knows what. ”  “The Constabulary had Drones up there last Friday, at our, our request, and have not reported anything untoward ” their special monthly call out used up, the moustache lamented. What would they do if unruly youths were romping? “The Drones didn 't go near them. I watched them, buzzing about all over the place never up the hill. ”  “The Contabulary assures me any concerns are rooted in nothing but fiction. It isn 't even switched on yet for mercys sake. Nevertheless ” he held a hand to ward off her protestation “a comment has been submitted regarding your noise complaint. ”   “They would say that, they 're ” her eyes grew wide “Them. ”  Julie prided herself on not being a fan of “Them. ” She 'd spent a significant portion of her youth standing up to them, attending protests specifically aimed at stopping the ever growing influence of them and, often semi clothed, smashing the windows of the official buildings of Them. As far as she was concerned they weren 't welcome around here. This was why Roger wanted better background checks.

---

Some Pointless Citizens were more Pointless than others. “I don 't know why you swallow everything they tell you Roger, the Constabulary isn 't the be all and end all. ”  “More like the Be All and Arsehole ” Jones and Julie hit a loud high five, they 'd come up with it over a bottle of wine last night, solidarity in fighting the power. “Who agreed to this mast Rog? Not me, not Jones, not even you Paul Bond ”  “Well I would have if they 'd-  “I 've been watching them at night ” the shadows deepened. “Ah, ah time Rog ” Naj pointed at his watch again, seductively, engulfing Jones, enticing her in with his rolling black curls and-   “After, after curfew? ”  “I 've been watching. As we all should be ” the finger included them all in the crime “Makes me sick just listening to them up there and its not even on yet. Think of the kids. ”  “I don 't think the government would- ” Hannah squeaked in the face of Julies umbridge. Jones like that word, umbridge. Ummmm bridge.

---

“I shan 't stand for it. ”  Roger sighed a sigh thats lived through crusades such as “I 'm sure those kids are listening to hip hop ” and “They let their dog piss on my bushes. ”  “Perhaps it would be pertinent to organise a visit, perhaps, perhaps someone from the Department of Psychoacoustics could provide us with, with a bit more information. Perhaps a demonstration. I 'll bring it, raise it with the Constabulary ” the moustache twitched “In the meantime, I would question the, question the sensibilities of openly questioning government policy at a Party Approved special interests meeting. ”  “All in the minutes Rog ” Shirley cackled. The finger lowered, finally. Julie stared round the room. “Whats the point in the Watch if we aren 't looking out for each other? ”  “Yes well ” Roger wouldn 't meet her eyes “Anybody, anybody else got anything they 'd like to cover? ”  Jones sent an unblinking stare around the room, beseeching them to keep their mouths shut. Hannah stood up. The bitch. “I just wanted to remind everybody about Mondays Boot Sale happening on the little green outside our house. All the proceeds are going to the community water fund ” she handed out some fliers.

---

Ten minutes later, after Paul Bond had finished telling Hannah how she could produce her own water with some polythene , Roger called an end to the meeting. Thirty seconds after that, Esmerelda Jones stepped out into the cold. The crowd roars. The music picks up, the guitar a wailing discordance, the heavy thump of the bass carrying it along in waves. Drums. The singer calls to arms the thousands watching. John Blard reads the crowd and pulls a filthy lick on his air guitar, climbing the sofa to get a better look at the writhing masses. Cheers, they were cheering along with every sound he made, bringing them along with him, settling into a rhythmic pulsing, drawing them in, breaking free with a yaaaa yaaa yaaa yaaaa. Trumpets. They sounded in perfect time as he tapped all up and down the neck of the guitar. And now the thumping rhythm, as he steps up to the microphone. And catches sight of himself in the mirror. And takes his headphones out. And has a quiet word with himself. Residential Zone 42 Designation Cloudtop View was once described by Greatest Britains Best Kept Designated Residential Zones as “largely unremarkable, other than all the goblins ”.

---

After a week of unhappy, confused, in some cases incandescent correspondence with the citizens of RZ42, this was downgraded to “unremarkable ”. Like many of the zonal neighbourhoods hastily fenced off post Tumult it consisted of blocks of two distinct types of house. There were the ones that were there before, them from the new build bubble, two and three beds with their nice little front garden bits, red bricks and coloured doors. Then, in the spaces that were left you had the one up one down Socially Allocated Domiciles, with their walls that wobbled in the wind and flammable windows. Emergency housing tossed together for the economic refugees reeling from a forty percent population drop and the inevitable downfall that followed. A half built childrens park sat just off to the side of the Community Centre, you could use the swings if you brought your own seat. Jones lit a cigarette and walked down Granville Lane, boots stomping extra hard in the freezing cold of July. The estate had four roads, Granville Road, Trotter Avenue, Larkin Street and Inspector Frost Lane. The first two were mostly the nice houses, generally considered the highest quality of home in Greatest Britain, even if the bathroom manufacturer had recently admitted to replacing silicone with frogspawn.

---

Frost and Larkin had most of the SADs, constructed largely of cardboard and prayers with their little energy windmills spinning all day every day. At the end of Larkin was a long dirt track surrounded by a field devoid of anything but cow shit and chain fencing, it lead up to Simcock Hill, the home of Julies death ray. Ugly soviet looking thing it was, looming over all them houses, a thin strand of metal topped by a hollow bronze sphere. Some other bits that looked like satellites hung off the sides of it, bit like a sonic screwdriver Jones thought, but massive and not being held by David Tennant. She made the turn from Granville onto Derek, boots making a satisfying crunch on the gritty tarmac. The temperature had dropped in the last few days, the first sparks of Winter setting frosty fire to the leafy piles of autumn, if she was being poetic about it. It must’ve been nice down Derek, spaced out a bit like, before they’d crammed SADs in either side of the formerly detached homes.

---

She passed the cosy lounges of huddled together families, glancing in to see faces lit up by Blackadder on the tv, dogs lolling all over sofas they weren 't supposed to be on, the Graysons slapping some bass as a family. Safe, it was. The best time, these twilight winter hours, when the suns gone down but the drone wasn 't out yet. She smoked her way down the last of her cigarette, got out her key, and let herself in to Number 8 Derek Avenue. “Oi twatface ” she shouted, scraping her shoes along the welcome mat. Welcome mat was a strong description, it was what you had left of a Welcome mat when all the welcomes gone away. “Do you not knock? Is that not a thing that you got taught? Shut the door its freezing ” footsteps stumbled across the landing. Jones pushed the door to and put the chain on. Thats it, keep the scary murderers outside, so they know he means business. “Since when do mates have to knock? You gave me a key, thats practically a constant invite ” she threw her coat over the banister.

---

“Literally any time post the 1980s ” John appeared from the top of the stairs, wearing pajamas, a dressing gown and a scowl, his dark greying hair plastered to his head, his angular jaw jutting out of his big face in annoyance “I told you you 've only got the key for emergencies, like if I fall down the stairs or have a heart attack or something. Do you want a brew? ”  “Yeah, and a wine. How would I know if you 'd fallen down the stairs to use the key? You wouldn 't be able to tell me. ”  “No ” said John, filling the kettle up too quickly and soaking the front of his pajama top “Shit. But if you did happen to come round you 'd be able to come in and find me, rather than the police having to kick the door in days after it happened to find me in desperate pain and covered in piss, or dead ” He put the kettle on the base thing, flicked it on and grabbed a bottle of wine. “Yeah but then I 'd have to use it to get in anyway.

---

The knocking wouldn 't matter see, unless I 'm just walking in theres no point me having a key. ”  “Fair point, give me the key back then ” he offered his hand, not in marriage like, just for the key back. “Nah, I like having a key, its useful, it means we can have chats like this. ”  John handed her a glass of wine, cup of tea and took his own brew into the living room. It was the same living room found in any of the nice actual brick houses in the estate, offensively neutral. The magnolia walls chimed perfectly with the grey sofa, the standard issue wall mounted tv staring out over a brown plastic coffee table slightly too short to comfortably reach for a drink from. John threw himself onto the sofa whilst Jones took her armchair facing the patio doors. “Whats happening then Jones? Any terrorists blowing up Rogers rhododendrons? A flower whos amusing name is usurped only by the Grellyfosh Flower.

---

Given the Grellyfosh ' propensity to drill its tendrils directly into the brain of anyone within a four foot radius of it it is far less common, and somewhat less actually funny. ”  “What you don 't read the newletter? ”  “If by read you mean put in the bin then yes. ”   “Bad man. Julie still wants to shag the tache off Roger and reckons Harmonys going to melt all our faces. Hannahs boring, Paul Bond. ”  “Paul Bond ” John nodded. “Roger asks after you, says he might ” she gulped “pop round to see you soon. Doesn 't like members of his flock he never sees. Think he wants you to join the Watch. Guess you 'll have to now oh well. ”  John snorted. In flagrant mockery of the Cloudtop Neighbourhood Watch Community Engagement Drive he hadn 't been to any of the Cloudtop Neighbourhood Watch Community Engagement Sessions. He hadn 't even given apologies for his absence. “Tell him, again, I 've got much better things to do, like counting my rice. ”  “I just think he misses you. You two must have had something really special before you stopped leaving the house ” she said, drinking a bit from her tea and a bit from her wine.

---

“I think me and him must have had three conversations ever, all on that doorstep over there ” he pointed at the door “One about joining the Watch, one about why I didn 't want to and one about how terribly terribly sorry he was to hear the news. ”  “Yeah I don 't really g- ”  “Oh, and one really pissed conversation nine years ago about how he gets his moustache so spiffing. I 'd rather that hadn 't happened but I do have a recommendation for moustache wax that I 'm never going to forget. ”  Jones sank into her seat, allowing the combination of tiny amounts of caffeine and alcohol to do almost nothing for her burgeoning headache. Trying to force John Blard out of his house to do something other than go to work was an irritating hobby for her. Like having a sore bit on your knee that won 't go away so you poke it, and it hurts, so you poke it some more, and it hurts more, but now you quite like it so at any given opportunity you 'll give it a poke despite not really remembering what the initial intention was with that first poke. “Bull cum ” John announced. “Bull? ”  “Cum.

---

He puts bull cum in his moustache, honest to god thats what he said. ”  “He does not put bull cum on his moustache ” she snorted “it wasn 't true the first time you told me and it isn 't true now. ”  “Bull cum Jones, right on the twiddly bits. Has it in these little vials so he never runs out. Stiffens up really nice ” John twiddled his imaginary moustache at her. “Oh fuck off ” Jones giggled “See this is exactly the kind of top insight we 're missing at the Neighbourhood Watch. I think even Julie might think twice about snogging him if she knew he had that plastered on his face ” she raised her eyebrows lasciviously and did a bit of a tongue waggle. It was a bit weird she thought in retrospect, and perhaps a bit too lascivious, but fuck it its her face she can do what she wants. Just how did Roger get the bull jizz? “Whats wrong with your face are you having a stroke? ”  “No piss off ” she took one gulp of wine, one gulp of tea.

“So is that why you 've come round, you on a mission from the Lord High General Moustache? ”  Jones raised an eyebrow “Oi I 'm on your permits, you 're paying for this privilege. ”  “You 're my free one. My only one actually. ”  “Really? Aww Blard. ”  “Don 't take it personally I wouldn 't have any if I could get away with it. ”  “Oi. You not cool with seeing me two days in a row? ”  “No its fine ” John sipped from his tea. “Mate imagine having to go the meetings on your own, imagine having to listen to what Hannahs baking this week, or Paul Bond. ”  “Paul Bond ” He 'd dealt with Paul Bond once, when on his walk home from work Paul had pointed out that the way he was walking wasn 't technically in accordance with the Social Order Act. “Paul Bond. ”  “You 've got Naj, Naj is alright. ”  “Oh he is lovely, but I can 't even tell if hes awake half the time. Besides, hes one of them. Couple of months ago he heard if potholes have got obscenities painted on them the council will sort them out quicker.

---

Now all he does is go around painting cocks on the road. ”  “That explains so much about something I 've been really confused by ” John shook his head “Ok, not Naj. What about … ” he cycled through the other members of the Watch he could remember “Shir …ley? ”  “Yeah right Shirley hates me, she told me to go back where I come from last week ” Jones took a big swig of wine “We went door listening the other day and she- ”  “Jones ” John backed away in horror. “Oh no. ”  “You 're one of them ” he pointed at her, Invasion of the Body Snatchers style. “I 'm one of them ” she squeezed her hands over he ears “Its not my fault its Community Service. ”  “How many times Jones? How many times have you twitched those curtains? Stood staring out into the street asking ” he affected what was supposed to be a west country farmers accent but was actually somewhat Cajun “who are these folk that be round here, riding their bikes, driving o 'er peoples cats. ”  “Ha! ” Jones liked funny voices “They 're dragging me in, this is why I need you coming with me, to keep me sane. ”  “Only got yourself to blame spliffy.

---

Besides I can 't, I 'm far too busy. ”  “Too busy writing down every way the news says you could die tomorrow? ”  “Kept me alive so far. ”  Jones stuck her tongue out. Recently she 'd come upon the idea that if she was going to force him to actually have a life it was going to have to be done in bits. Muted iron grey skies, rain that cant be arsed to be real rain but still relentlessly pisses it down, wind fast enough to feel it, combined with the sun somehow shining straight in your face to really complete the triple whammy of mildly irritating precipitation. ---

Budget constraints meant checkpoints were staffed during office hours, leaving the gates open and unmanned for the majority of the day. The turnstile had broken some months ago, Jones assured him Roger was all over the Constabulary about it. When its comes to crime and terrorists, its the thought that counts. He steeled himself as he entered the In Betweens. He furiously ignored the homeless man hovering halfway down the hill. Not out of any great emnity towards the homeless, John Blard stoically avoided any unprepared human interaction rich or poor. You never know who might want to know how you 're feeling, or murder you in a nail bomb explosion. The houses start to huddle in halfway down the hill, boarded up terraces, desolate front gardens and shells of abandoned cars, punctuated by the occasional bedraggled denizen making their furtive way through the day. He took his life in his hands every time he descended the hill. Mask on. End of hill. Walk down main street. Stop, check road, two people, one looking at wall, why, why, moving away, fine, other head down, no threat. Check road. No cars. Walk into road, quickly, get to other side. Stop. People close, keep to other side of path for maximum distance, other crossed the road away from me. No threat.

---

Carry on. Small group, mostly non-threatening looking, one has a child, good, safe, other has a sports bag, could be a bomb, walk on left side of group to minimise impact should they detonate. Keep looking ahead, don 't offend by your actions, keep walking. Checkpoint in thirty seconds. One more person walking. Female, head up. Hands on show. No threat. Shes coughed. Pause. Wait for dispersal. Go. Safe. The Commercial Zone checkpoint was the bastard child of biological security and unambitious budgets, all wire and corroded shipping containers torn from their jetset life, welded into something between a prison walkway and a fast food restaurant. Algae infested wooden barricades from the time of the Tumult formed the edges of the enclave, yellowing posters calling for new members to a long won political cause nailed to them. Local Crows had inscribed the Roman numeral for four on every fourth post, not that they existed, that sort of thinking would get you locked up. John took a ticket from a tattered raffle ticket book and shuffled into the corridor of fencing. In front of him were mesh gates and a temperature scanner, if he was lucky enough to be just right, it opened onto a body scanner. He was reliably informed the scanners were no harm, mostly magnetic.

---

Large plate metal gates blocked the exit onto the bus platform, a spotlight embedded in the far wall shining out into the mist of rain. A container above the gates had been converted into a guard room, a CRT display hung off the fence, flickering on the number 72. He looked how a pork pie feels, the ruddiness of December cold and alcoholism flooding his face. “Hi Frankwell ” Raymond Frankwell, a guard friendlier than you want the man between you and the terrorists to be, a man whos life had been defined the night someone told him he smelled of kebabs. “There we are John! ” he waved him through “Same time again tomorrow? ”   “Every day Frank. ”  John shuffled into the boarding area for the Number Seventy Two bus, joining what loosely resembled a queue of other well to dos and ne 'er do wells. The platform he stood on was a long row of raised concrete overlooking a road pocked with bullet holes, the stony debris of uprising shoved to the sides, rubble forming a low barricade at each edge. Bit like a train platform but without the rails and not a single broken vending machine. More of the light metal grilling separated the proles from the road, the only opening a six-foot ramp hovering out above it. This one had a way of holding his gun just so that made him silently crap his pants. There might be no money for more than one bus service a day, but at least the guards looked intimidating. A great honking announced the arrival of the bus. The steel shutters protecting the bus stop from the outside world ground into life, producing a noise that could best be mimicked by dragging the worlds heaviest chair across the worlds metallest floor. Flashing lights revolved around poles. The decaying bus entered the hangar, coughing its way to a stop on specialist tyres designed to cope with a road system that in parts resembled the surface of the moon. The windows were all steel reinforced letting just a sliver of light in on either side. They 'd removed half the seats in all public transport to add a bit of distance between everyone, if you looked closely at the back of it you could actually see the very faint outline of the Megabus mascot that once adorned it. The queue queued. “Passes out ” The guard dragged the gate to the side, opening the way to the bus. John already had his pass in hand, gormless face staring back at him from the top right corner of the plastic card.

---

Alright? As previously discussed, this is John. This is Denman and Howe. You remember the commercials? Private Eyes? You know, the one for the Drones, Hall and Oates, We 're watching you. John was into his ninth year at Denman and Howe, a job move borne out of necessity and a subconscious dedication to mid seventies soft rock. It was okay, a lot better than his preceding role in Mega Dairy 3, the udders had made him pensive. The Denman and Howe building was a building within which there were offices.

---

Once described by an onlooker as “probably the most depressing building I 've ever seen ”, it had been built in the distant pre-Tumult past, when brown concrete and Stalag chic were still in fashion. For a more physical representation get a cardboard box and fill it with as many pictures of sad animals as you can. Stare at it. Breath it in. Get it a bit wet. There you go, a warehouse of human misery. For all its aesthetic beauty, it had the massive benefit of being secure. A short walk from the transport hub kept potential risks to a minimum, with a Checkpoint into it that, whilst much less impressive than the district gateways, had yet to permit any scimitar wielding murderers. One of the guards had smiled at John once which he wasn 't sure about, but you 've got to play the game, make friends, influence people. To get to his desk John had to go through a turnstile. Loads of turnstiles actually. The main entrance, the corridors, the kitchen, even the toilets had turnstiles until Harris shit himself when he forgot his pass. At last count the turnstiles outnumbered the employees three to one. Whilst the current terror threat for Realist Party advertising agencies was low, you could never be too careful.

---

John was safe in the knowledge that on the day that they came Denman and Howe would be ready, safely behind their shitload of turnstiles. His desk was located right over by the window, redundant given he couldn 't see out of said window due to the iron bars all across it. He did occasionally get a breeze through the piss poor sealant round the edges, sometimes it even dissipated the smell you find in every office space, that pervasive blend of farts and disappointment, emanating from the pores of all the people trapped in here with the psychopaths that actually enjoyed coming to work   The psychopaths smelt of rhubarb when you got close to them. They most probably bathed in it, a big psychopath bath, rubbing the rhubarb all over each other. . There were just six of them in a Denman and Howe office built decades ago for seventy five people, workforces decimated as they were D and H were the forth largest RP advertisers in the country. ---

You could just about see the people opposite you, but only if you did that uncomfortable motion where you 're not stood up but you may as well be but if you did stand up it would be weird so you do the weird chair rise up thing. That 's the one. The one you just did there, where you sort of raised your shoulders up but didn 't actually move. There we go. Peering they call it. The design was to encourage limited communications with your colleagues, the not standing not sitting limbo many found themselves in daily was, according to eminent data analysts, the optimum position with which to maximise the productivity of a workplace.~  Each desk was laid out the same, permitting a keyboard, a rotary phone, a roller ball mouse, an enormous desktop computer with CRT monitor and a single A4 framed picture of those important to you. You know, to remind you of why you 're giving up your life to stare at the same meaningless screen day in day out. The little plaque above his workstation told John that he was a Marketing Caption Executive, a role a computer used to do for a lot less money, when they were allowed to.

---

There was no way he could have stopped the spin so he didn 't go down that route, he was going too fast, he 'd have had to put his hand out to arrest it and that would have a) hurt a bit and b) made a right noise. Parts of the field were littered with mangled streetlights and left over fencing, the countryside bits of everywhere had been the worst victims of the Zoning Initiative. Huge swathes of greenery were now cut in half by sweeping curves of concrete foundations and fencing, encircling entire neighbourhoods to connect back up at the various checkpoints along its length. Each zone varied in size dependent on population density, number of houses, amenities, whether or not they had had enough fence on the given day and just thought fuck it, here will do. ---

Dotted around the park were little clearings housing makeshift shelters and pop up tents, temporary homes for those that couldn 't find a suitable abandoned terrace to make their bed in. Or those that just preferred the outdoors, this is where Jones would 've been, where she could smell the flowers and listen to the birds. She waved to the Uddins as she passed their little family camp. Bramble Close was just the other side of the park, over the old canal bridge, through a fence and into the old terraces. Jones followed the path of flattened grass well worn by the inhabitants of the In Betweens over the old canal. Beneath the bridge the waterways were clogged with junked flatscreen televisions and smashed up iPads, when landfills had become landfulls the dried up canal beds had been the logical places to junk all of the newly banned technology. Last time she was this way she 'd climbed down to have a look, hoping to find an iPad with a bit of charge and Super Axe Man installed. All she 'd found was cracked, dead black screens and bird shit. Her old house was an old back to back, orange brick and rotting white wood frames at the end of a long row of terraces.

---

She 'd sorted the gardens out on her last visit, free of charge, the hardy perennials were doing well. Someone had pried back the boards since she was last here, probably trying to get out of the rain, or nick whatever trinkets had been forgotten in the move. Unlucky for you tea leaves but she had bugger all in the first place. Rotted wooden boards hung limply from the window, giving a glimpse into a life long left behind. She could see the old gray carpet, mildewed by the rain, the stain left in the living room wall when she 'd painted a geometrically perfect circle in order to create a physical manifestation of her inner eye so that she could converse with the machine elves running the world, the bracket where the telly used to be. Nothing left in there but ghosts and giggles. She hopped the gate, the bolt had rusted shut forever ago, into a long thin garden, at the end a tiny strip of grass elevated above a brown stone patio, a rusted old deck chair still atrophying next to an empty terracotta plant pot.

---

She walked to the end of the garden and sat down on the grass next to a paw print stone that read “Bollo. ”  “Hey Bollo ” she broke out into a smile “You been a good boy? I miss you you know. ”  Bollo had been with her everywhere. All the way from her first student house in Aberystwyth to researching in Minsk, always there with a happy licky face and a wagging tail. He was twelve when he died, an arthritic old cream labrasomething with much more interest in cheese than going for walks. She could still feel his big stupid head and smell his dusty fur when he 'd bump her for attention. She 'd buried a big part of herself in this plot, when she was relocated she 'd promised to come and see him whenever she could. She always came away with the bittersweet sadness of perfect memories and the impossibility that she 'd ever get them back. Oh, and a couple of buds of weed from the stuff she had stashed in the gap between the doorstep and the wall. She laid her head back, put a hand on the stone, pushed any thoughts of missing Julies from her mind and remembered her dog for a bit.

Waking up in John Blards spare room was an unpleasant experience. It wasn 't the alcohol, Jones hadn 't had a hangover once in her life because she was an awful human being and very glad of it. It wasn 't the bed neither, it was much comfier than the fifteen year old reclaimed mattress and pile of blankets she slept under.

---

It was warm in here, Blard had the heating on during his alloted power hours, in case there was a sudden drop in temperature outside that lead to instant frostbite for those not in well insulated, adequately temperatured houses. No, it was the malaise, thats what it was. Nothing to ruin your wake up like a general pervading sense of good old dread. You wouldn 't call it haunted, not exactly, there was just this vibe that you might wake up with a dead eighteen fifties housewife hovering above your bed lamenting. An aura that suggested something not really there might whisper in your ear. The spare room was the only one where you 'd find any evidence that Blard had ever been married, a dusty shrine to a life he wouldn 't talk about. On the top of a white flatpack chest of drawers was a picture of John Blards wife, somewhere pretty, rolling hills in the background, like back home. Ericas round face grinned out at you from it, bottle blonde hair wild in the breeze. It was an odd feeling, seeing that alien happiness frozen in time. Nice, melancholic, an emotional mosquito caught in the amber of reality. Niceancholic. Nah, no good that one. She could go for Jurassic Park though. She rolled out of bed.

---

In the corner of the room was a box. Just a clear plastic box, the sort shops used to replace all their stock with when it wasn 't one of a hundred different occasions. Out of sheer nosiness Jones had investigated it once to find stacks of scrapbooks filled with flowers, case studies on minor civil land ownership cases and far, far too many pictures of dogs. No pictures of them together though, John probably got rid of them all. Blard was the sort of bloke to pretend a life defining human being had never existed, not out of malice, just sheer inability to accept reality. He didn 't talk about her, other than accidentally. This box was as good an introduction as her and Mrs Blard would ever have. Jones liked her. She got dressed and floated down the stairs, rubbing her eyes awake. She nicked some bread and butter from the kitchen and left. Slowly. She eyed the sky suspiciously for any signs of her Drone friend, stamped a bit of warm into her feet, then set off to Julies to kick the fucking door down because seriously where the fucking hell was her friend. The kitchen stank of fish.

---

For someone to break into the back garden of course, its what friends do. She 'd planted them herself, three hours they took, best trade for a shower she 'd ever made. The garden was entirely free of Julies, no signs of a single one. Her gray rattan furniture was still dragged into a neat pile in the corner, the lawn a slightly too long wintry bog. Jones pressed her face to the kitchen window peering under the semi closed blinds. The part of her brain expecting an horrific scene of an old, friendly womans head smashed in, brains painting the room in a thick crimson ichor was, happily enough, completely wrong. ---

It came from Julies honeymoon in Bermuda   On the way back through customs they 'd found out that hidden within the feet of the statue was a small amount of heroin, not loads like but enough to take the edge off. Three days in a Bermudan jail later a young man named Jose Pedrosa stepped forward to admit it was his gear. He was dead apologetic and had never meant to get any tourists into trouble, he never expected anyone to buy the stupid gorp faced monstrosity. Julie and Ray were terribly thankful to him and even discussed staying in touch to help pay for his treatment to get him on the straight and narrow, maybe even have him over for Christmas one year. What better than friends in Bermuda eh! Jose was executed six weeks after they left the country, but it was still a great conversation starter whenever anyone asked “Wheres this frog from Julie? ” . She loved that frog, she talked to it, it wasn 't close to all she had left of Ray, she had boxes of photo albums and football programmes up in her loft, but it was her favourite bit.

---

They went for good money down the In Betweens, between the crap TV signal and all day Tony Bingehound they 'd pay a lot for any escape. And he had. He 'd sat at her bedside, day after day, listening to the sound of her breathing, the morbid metronome by which he measured the rest of his life. One in, one out, one step closer to who the fuck knows what, crippling loneliness with a hefty side of lifelong misery. Becoming that bloke whos wife has died. Watching the children they never had outside of his head die with her. Her becoming his wife that died, instead of being the person that was so much bigger than anyone he 'd ever met. At first she just started to forget things, little things like locking the front door or turning the oven off, things that normal people forgot but Erica Blard would never. She 'd tell him stories that never happened, as though he was the one imagining things.

---

At first he thought she was taking the piss, telling him about how next door had been round a couple of weeks ago to chat about the fence, but they didn 't share a fence and the neighbours were both in hospital. Or telling him she 'd finished a case, but her client had been calling the office for the past three days asking why she wouldn 't answer the phone. At first he wrote the clumsiness off as stress, a broken glass or walking into doors, the occasional fall off the bed that they both found hilarious at the time, utterly sinister in the retrospective afterglow of her illness. Then she walked in front of a car, and that wasn 't funny. At first a brain tumour is the kind of news that leaves your life ringing, that carries a physical body, it walks into the room and punches you in the face. But hey. Operable. The prognosis was actually very positive. Caught it pretty early, course of chemo to shrink it down, terrifying face-peeling off surgery to get it out but don 't worry Mrs Blard, theres every reason you 'll go on to live a long and happy life. You 're young, you 'll bounce back. She did bounce back.

---

At first things went as well as they possibly could have. She had her surgery and her treatment, work were brilliant, oh weren 't they brilliant, take all the time you both need, no rush, except for you John, a bit of a rush but not for the first couple of weeks though eh. And then Uncategorised Virus Number Five. The latest in post Tumult hammer blows to a country just wobbling back to its feet. At first it was arm breakingly obvious that she was going to be vulnerable. At first it was easy enough to keep her inside while the world figured how to cope with yet another Pandemic. Disinfect the shopping, no friends, no family, but its OK because no dying, no widowing. John made himself a makeshift airlock. In the door, spray yourself down with disinfectant, clothes straight in the wash and into the shower. No touching for at least half an hour until he 'd scraped the very last bit of dirt from underneath his fingernails. She was convinced he was overreacting, as was he. But you could never be too careful, because he didn 't want to become that bloke whose wife has died. And he didn't want her to become dead.

Walking through a supermarket when Cynthias just let off a huge sneeze into the air because oh I cant wear a mask deary it steams up my glasses was death. Walking in the countryside was death. Shaking hands with a prospective client was death. Drinking wine in a bar with friends was death. At first they were winning. The problem with At First is that it isn 't In The End. In the end seizures wracked her body, this worming writhing cancer reviving, resolutely growing up and out through her brain, stealing away everything about her. In the end she started coughing, her body still cancer sick and weak. As wave after wave of death and disease swept the country they hunkered together in that spare room, John cradling her head as he prayed that she got back up from this one, that they didn 't have to expose her to the hospitals full of the near dead and choking. In the end she didn 't wake up. In the end she was taken in an ambulance. In the end she couldn 't fight them both.

In the end John sat at her bedside, listening to the sound of the love of his life drowning in her own mucus, praying to a God he didn't think existed to do something, anything, to save her. Jones slumped to the ground. Her bones stopped vibrating, the voice abandoned her. Set IT free. Every muscle was burned, torn apart, the pain soared up and out of her, releasing her, a harmonious discord blaring out into the sky.

---

The sound left her, replaced with a fleeting euphoria, only to be swallowed by the cold, hard certainty of what came next. She saw herself as a little girl in Conwy County, heard her moms mischievous laugh, smelt her dads rusty old wheelchair, she thought of the first time she smoked a cigarette, the first time she drank a beer, kissed a boy, kissed a girl, rode a pony, lost a dog, lost a grandparent, got stuck in a relationship she shouldn 't have, got too drunk, went to Minsk, fought a ship captain, survived the Pulpos, flew to Spain, climbed a mountain, moved house, got a tattoo, forgot her best friend, dyed her hair black, got stuck on a train, fucked in the snow, met her best friend, wrote a letter, discovered some flowers in Minsk, lost Bollo, smoked more cigarettes, drank more wine, was stroppy was happy was sad, was a lot more than angry and very in love, saw a whale, punched a gropey arsehole in a pub, got her head stuck in some railings, went to her sisters wedding, started school, heard a song for a funeral, looked for Julie, got hit in the head, had a bomb strapped to her chest, that fucking fucking fucking sound. Came here. The End.
