“I thought there would be more ” she said. There is a sound that precedes the beginning of everything, and the end of everything else. Boom. PART TWO  ACT 2: THE WALRUS    9  ACT TWO The Walrus 10    Sit. Stare. Sit. Stare  Awake. Always awake. TV. News. Terror. Esmerelda Jones. The Cloudtop Bomber. Her face was everywhere, staring out from every news bulletin, on the front of every newspaper. They 'd found the roughest looking picture of her that they could, dark hair, darker eyes and an admittedly sinister sort of haunted look. The black and white TV in the tiny room upstairs in the Big Deal did her no favours, she 'd hated that photo, it was taken years ago after a heavy night in Minsk involving a Columbian poker player and a tortoise. “-and her accomplice Julie Cooper in an attack that has shaken Greatest Britain- ”  Sit. Stare. Sit. Stare. The Inquisition found pictures of John Barnard Jenkins on her walls, FWA propaganda like “Y Gelyn Drws Nesaf ” and “Sais marw yw Sais da ” in her bed side table. Her living room had a beheaded statue of King William in it for fucks sake. It didn 't feel like Jones, she loved a royal and she didn 't even know where Llangollen was.

---

Her and her accomplice, known conspiracist Julie Cooper, Cooper gone missing, underground, Jones a martyr to the free welsh nation. Even now, the TV was playing that video of Jones singing the Welsh national anthem at a rugby game circa who knows when, superimposed over the burning wreckage of the Community Centre. Sit. Stare. Sit. Stare. Three catatonic days he had sat and stared at the screen in the corner of this relic of a bedroom, waiting to expire, a stained mattress for company. At some points he was vaguely aware of Reza coming in to check on him, force him to drink some water, nibble at the corners of whatever Jemima had slapped in some bread. He didn 't see the point in prolonging things. Sometimes he 'd blink and two hours had passed and he was once more staring into the eyes of Esmerelda Jones as the news dissected her life, picking out the juicy bits, the bits that made her sound like a suicide bomber. The only thing worse than seeing Jones ' face as the representation of all that was evil in the world today was seeing his own. Sit. Stare. Sit. Stare.

---

Every couple of hours they 'd show a blown up image of his semi masked face looking into the Five Eyes at the bus stop. Mr John Blard, 8 Derek Avenue. Have you seen this big faced man? May be going under the alias of John Bomb. Esmerelda Jones closest confidante, her only living permit. Wanted for immediate Inquisition. Anti Citizen John. “Were they an item? Most certainly having it away, but one thing was for certain, he must have known something was going on, it was most probably his fault, he must have been in on it, he could be armed and dangerous ” was what Tony Bingehound had said, as he bounced around outside Johns house with a microphone, shoving it in the face of any apprehensive residents he could corner. It was the first time John had ever seen his spam coloured face. He was much younger than John had imagined, like a baby grown to full size, slapped in the face and drunk. John didn 't feel very dangerous. He felt numb. Pointless. His own personal apocalypse, a dead best friend and wanted for a terror he didn 't commit. Bit of a loner, the news said, kept himself to himself, didn 't read the newsletter, the usual.

---

He 'd seen enough local terror attacks to know how it went for the known associates, a trip to the Mad House, maybe a guest spot on the Denunciation if it really captured the countries imagination which, of course, this one had. Pretty young woman turned against the nation that provided everything for her, local watch members poisonous snakes all along. Sit. Stare. Sit. Stare. The Inquisition were door to door across Zone 42. The Graysons were made to kneel in the street at gunpoint and read their rights, known associates of terror after she 'd sorted them some creeping ivy a few months ago. Tina Bond wasn 't allowed to grieve for her husband, she 'd been seen in Julie Coopers house two weeks prior and she could be the key to uncovering the real culprits, the masterminds behind the attacks. Only one thing could save the country, Harmony, Peace Through Programming. If only the mast had been at full power, this could never have happened. This could never be allowed to happen again. There was a thud at the door, bits of decayed blue door frame showering the mouldy carpet. “Last call Zone man. You don 't have to go home but you can 't stay here ” said Reza from the other side of the door. Sit.

---

Stare. Sit. Stare. Thud. “Can 't I? ”   “You can do what you want man I just like that line. Come on, we need your house keys. ”  John groaned and hauled himself out of his mouldy corner of misery to pull the door open. “What for? ”  “We need those codes man, we 're going. Tonight. You can come with us, if you want. Join us man, cause some shit. ”   “You can 't go to my house, they 'll think I 'm a terrorist. ”  “They already do. ”  “Fair point ” John held out a bunch of too many keys for one door “Keys. ”  “You really just gonna stay here? Got a space in the car for one more, I 'll let you play some Hall and Oates. ”  John blinked slowly, his insomniac eyes throbbing with the motion. He turned away and hunkered back down in the corner, staring at the half static screen. Reza lingered in the door way for a while, hands tapping a rhythm against his hips. Finally he frowned, pocketed the keys and disappeared down the crumbling hallway of the Big Deal. Somewhere on the periphery of John Blards awareness he heard a car pulling away outside. Sit. Stare. Sit. Stare.

---

On the crackling TV screen the face of Esmerelda Jones dissolved away to show the footage of Zone 42 in the immediate aftermath of the attacks. The camera panned across the decimated Community Centre, Drones buzzing above the scene, bees mourning the loss of a hive. Some specialist Drones sprayed water cannons at a fire that had thought it was going to be a blaze but hadn 't got very far. A cavalcade of sirens rang in the distance. What remained could no longer be described as a building, now it was a hole with upward aspirations, bits of steel rods jutteing out of the wreckage, clinking and plinking as the fires died down. Chunks of rubble had been flung up into the air and strewn across the remnants of the area, glass shards mixing into the chaotic rain. The entrance to the building was somehow the only part left standing, the rest collapsed in on itself after the blast. The camera zoomed closer. Nothing could have survived the carnage. Closer. And yet there was movement. Stop. From the rubble appeared a finger, working its way out of the tomb. Then a fist, grasping at the debris around it. An arm. A face. A moustache.

---

The reception of the Minister of Peaces personal chambers was really, really quite remarkable, opulent in the most leather kind of way. Cherry red walls and waxy fascias, inset with metal studs, the kind of plush comfort you can only get from the hides of the most endangered animals. One must look past the battered corners, the time worn stitching and cracks in the dark mahogany doors, the hum coming from behind them. Look instead to the power of governance the very furniture exuded. Roger Harvey breathed deeply of that old money musk, freshly prepared moustache rigid and proud. “Shouldn 't be too much longer Mr Harvey. ”  “Thank, thank you my dear ” he nodded stiffly back at the receptionist, as much as his neck brace would allow him to. Damnable thing was interfering with both his pomp and his ceremony, conspiring with the ghastly sling wrapped around his arm and eye patch to present him to the leader of the country as some sort of pirate. Finally a return to the halls of power, even if it was whilst looking like a man, a man called Ahab. Still. What was an arm and an eye to be back here, the home of the Inquisition.

---

His visit to the Ministry of Peace   The Madhouse if you had no respect was born of a whirlwind of publicity. For days he had languished in an IC Unit in Medical Zone 8, receiving the sort of medical care only rumoured to exist, the sort banned under the Realist regime. A long miscounted number of skin grafts to his ruined face and days of reconstructive surgery on his now ninety percent metal arm had passed by in a haze of anaesthesia. The memory of that night was like a, like a cobweb in a sandstorm. He remembered the sound, he remembered her face, and he remembered being thrown across the room. He remembered the agony of digging himself out of the rubble with one useless arm, the aching numb of the right side of his face. He remembered the stinging lights that shone in his face, the rough hands and shocked voices, repulsed faces dragging him away from the last vestiges of the fire, delivering him into the painless void of the back of an ambulance. When he truly woke up he was famous. One doctor mentioned the, the mental scars, PTSD they called it, but he didn 't have much truck with that. Roger knew shellshock, and he knew that he didn 't get it.

---

If he shut his eye he could still see the look on Esmerelda Jones ' face as she was blown apart by a bomb strapped to her chest, which was, was unpleasant, but you didn 't see three tours without generating some nightmare fuel. His moustache twitched unhappily at the thought. Its OK, he told it. It 'll all be alright. He 'd woken up in a shining white sterile room filled with inefficiently large Get Well Soon cards, a whole florist worth of bouquets and sixteen large stuffed bears. And one watermelon from a hopeful, desperate, yet still sympathetic well wisher. The window out into the corridor was blocked by what, on first inspection appeared to be a well dressed fridge, but was later cleared up to be a heavy set member of the Inquisition. In the corner of the room sat a well put together lady in deep conversation with thin air. Once she 'd noticed his confused observance she 'd rung for a nurse, and, and following a lengthy wellness check involving a surprising moment with a thermometer the lady explained to him that she was Felicity Scrope, she was from the government, and we 'd like to work with you Mr Harvey. Supposedly he 'd become something of a minor celebrity during his coma.

---

She showed him the papers from the past few days, The Unsinkable Jolly Roger, War Hero Harvey Cheats Death. There he was on the front in his military pomp, his uniform weighed down by medals and the flag of Greatest Britain flying in the background. She turned the battered old TV on and showed him the rolling news coverage of reporters stood outside the hospital, the crowd keeping vigil behind barriers, the news ticker scrolling with updates on his condition. He got to see first hand the uncoiled joy when news reached the outside that he had woken up, that he was fine. The cameras showed the ripple as the news hit the crowd, people punching the air and embracing. It was really quite, quite touching. The government couldn 't let the service of such a brave man go to waste in this time of national adversity. There 'd be an official position in it for him. He was only too happy to help, once he was up and back on his feet of course, just say, just say the word and he was there. Which was good, Felicity said, because she never said she was asking. The press conference when he was released from hospital was simulcast across the country on television and radio.

---

The outpouring of elation was the closest thing England had seen to a football crowd since the Tumult, grown men and women jumping up and down chanting Walking in a Harvey Wonderland. Once they 'd calmed down came the carefully prepped for questions. No, he hadn 't suspected The Cloudtop Bomber, just showed it could be anyone. Yes, perhaps the signs were there and he was a damn fool not to notice them. Peace through programming. Now here he sat in his best suit, shoes shined so as to reflect those rays of light that are beyond the spectrum of human observation, ready to do, do anything he could to help burn out the scourge that had tainted his own neighbourhood watch, that had poisoned the minds of those he 'd once held close. He 'd even used the pot of special moustache wax he 'd been saving for his funeral. Damned expensive stuff. The intercom on the reception desk bonged with a pleasant little bell sound. The receptionist lifted a little old style receiver to her ear. “Yes Mr Baker.

---

Thank you Mr Baker ” she put the phone down “Mr Baker will see you now. ”  Roger sprang to his feet, back stiff and head held as high as his neck would allow, at attention and ready to march. “Thank, thank you my dear ” he had to hold back the salute. The hum in here was deafening, it vibrated Rogers teeth and sent sickening reverberations through his empty eye socket. The room was wide, brown and wainscoted, a perfectly normal office, were it not for the personal touches added to it by The Snake Ian Baker. A jar of green fluid sat on a cocobolo desk suspended half a Pulpo, stitched back together like a repaired knapsnack. Acoustic foam covered one side of the room whilst stretched across the ceiling was a mess of wires leading down into a bank of audio mixers. A bank of speakers hung from the ceiling, six of them all in a, in a row. Baker floated above a melee of dials, his heavily stained white lab coat flapping as he turned this and flipped up that. H hummed constantly with no consistent tune, bits and pieces of songs sewn together that should never have been, impossible to follow.

---

His eyes were bright with manic energy as he fizzed between the laptops set up on a picnic table in the corner showing a bouncing frequency reading. The hum rose, made one feel, feel quite tranquil. “How do you feel? ” said Baker. “Quite, quite peaceful sir. ”   “It was supposed to be apathy. We can 't seem to set the bass right ” his voice was stilted and high pitched, a far cry from the practised sibilant lilt he used in interviews “Back to the Think Tank ” Baker stared, one eye twitching, tongue working frenetically across his lips, each feature of his face moving independently of the rest. He was slender, his dark eyes deep set in a slim, square face, his short black hair sticking out in six separate directions. He turned his head on its side and took a long deep breath in through his nose. He moved closer, unblinking. “And who is this we see before us? ”   “Roger, Roger Harvey sir ” he clapped his heels together “Reporting as per Miss Scrope Sir ” but Baker had already spun back to his readouts, his straight back stance twanging like a band saw. “Significantly sub standard symphony, a wasted effort ” he twisted a dial and the hum died.

---

He moved towards Roger, his movements uneven and undulating to offer his hand, nostrils sniffing at the air. His handshake was clammy, cold and weak, a wet fish at the end of a broomstick. “Harvey. Harvey. Yes superb, Harvey Harvey ” he released Rogers hand from his trout grip and rolled out a shiny red leather chair from behind the desk, stacked high with yellowing papers and an array of used cardboard coffee cups. He scattered the mass of garbage across the office floor. “Yes, yes, yes you are he. You must tell us all about it ” he patted the seat, eyes fixed on Roger “Chop. ”  Roger took his seat, Baker excitedly shunted bits of wiring and stacks of paper from the desk and coiled into a one wheeled seat opposite. He sat lopsided, gently vibrating as he stared at Roger, flexing his fingers. “So do tell, do tell. What was it like. What did it sound like. What did she sound like. ”   “Who, who sir? ”  “The dead woman ” Baker jolted backwards slightly, he hummed a couple of bars of an unknown song “You were there correct? ”  This must be a test. Roger was the man for tests. “She was shouting in Welsh sir, something, something about a free welsh people.

---

Thats all I remember, before the, before the blast ” and the look in her eyes as the sound stopped but no, that was in the dream, that wasn 't what had happened she was, she was a terrorist. Baker pursed his lips into a barely visible line and hissed out a long breath. “No, no, no not the stories Scrope has you reading, no, not her words, her sounds ” he kicked at the desk “How did she move, was she in pain? How do you feel? Do you still hear it? ”   Movements like a puppet and terror in her eyes. A sound like a god crying. But that wasn 't what happened. A bad person did a bad thing to good people. “She, she walked in sir. She had a bomb ” Baker nodded along “She was speaking in Welsh and she- ”   “A simple simple simple question ” Roger stayed still and silent in his chair “Insignificant in the scheme of things.

---

To better, Mr Harvey. ”  “I am here to serve sir, sir, whatever you need, I 'm your willing subject ” he cleared his throat, steeling himself “and if I might add sir I truly, truly had no idea of either Watch members true leanings, yes Julie might have had her views on Harmony but none of us, none of us could have foreseen what was going to happen. I am more than, more than happy to bear my brunt of responsibility, I 'll gladly submit myself for Inquisition should the, should the Peace Ministry see fit to make an example. ”  Bakers tongue flickered, tasting the air around him. Roger braced for judgement. “You will lead the Denunciation, to not put a smile like yours to the big event would be such a shame. ”  “Sir. I 've never, never been for one public speaking sir. ”  “And yet supposedly you serve. Some time spent with The Inquisition should give you that fire back. Such a shame you didn 't see the snakes around you Mr Harvey. ”  “Yes, yes sir ” his moustache drooped in spite of himself.

---

Chin up Harvey, better to take your licks than fight it, he was as much at fault as any terrorists, a failure to Zone 42 “I 'll report myself for arrest at once Sir. ”  A slow smile slunk onto Bakers face “Oh my no Mr Harvey. You 're here to serve. You shall be an Inquisitor, yes, let us give you an insight into the sort of venom festering at the heart of your home. ”  Baker produced a desk phone from somewhere within the bureaucratic maelstrom of a desk, the microphone hanging out of one end of it “Stanley. See that Mr Harvey finds his way, theres a fellow ” he returned the phone to its paper covered grave “Sayonara, Mr Harvey. We have such work for you. ” Everything was decided by s think-tank apparently - that think-tank is literally a brain in a big tank     The think tank, its escaping   The world is literally taken over by a think tank at the end, h gok is the think tank. IAN BAKER IS JUST DOING WHAT THE THINK TANK SAYS HE SHOULD. HES BEEN TAKEN OVER BY THE THINK TANK, HE IS A VESSEL FOR THE THINK TANK. IT DEPARTMENT IS WHERE THE THINKTANK IS HELD. WE DON 'T GO TO IT, SPECIAL CLEARANCE.

---

COMPUTERS AND THE LIKE? UNDER LOCK AND KEY OF COURSE. UNAUTHORISED TECHNOLOGY. “Tea two sugars Rog ” Stanley jostled Rogers hand as he handed over a cardboard cup that had come into this world expecting to hold hot liquids but was positive this was taking it a bit too far “Careful lad, still a bit sore that. ”  “What, what happened to it? ”  “Got bit by a dog, Welsh terrier, vicious little monsters ”. Roger had taken an instant liking to Stanley, he was clearly a man who, who got things done, a man not short of a few medals in his lifetime. An induction into the Peace Ministry with a bona, bona fide Inquisitor. Roger had thought this feeling to be dead to the glass in his leg, yet, yet here he was, back amongst the throng, within the heart of those committed to bringing peace to the zones of Greatest Britain. The Ministry of Peace, dubbed The Madhouse by the disrespectful, was a repurposed sanitarium, a sprawling Victorian complex six stories high made of orange bricks and creeping ivy.

---

Hand picked post Tumult by Minister for Peace Ian Baker, it housed his most advanced scientific projects, the ones that really delved deep into how to control a nation of people that have just now toppled a government and are getting all together too full of themselves. Not one for PR, Baker was undeterred by the sense within government that this was a surefire way to come across as an absolutely mad bastard. If anything it was a feature, from his point of view there wasn 't another building in the world with completely sound proof rooms, or a ready made hollowed out underground lair, not for these prices. Even the Ministry of Peace had a budget. Each of the main buildings six floors housed a different department in experimental peace keeping. There was the Department of Confessions on floor 3, full of rows of cells housing dissidents of all shapes and sizes, all scum of course but diverse scum, you couldn 't be, couldn 't be picky with peace. This was where political terrorists, the disagreeable, the layabouts and criminals were brought to confess, to implicate others and, ultimately, to be punished. Opposite the cells the walls were lined with booths, empty but for a restraining chair and a camera, correction could only begin with a full, lifelong confession.

---

A steady stream of the unwashed were dragged from the cells by the burgundy uniformed guards of the Inquisition, some to the confessionals, others down, down ,disappearing into the underground of Psychoacoustics. “Fuller than I 've ever seen it ” said Stanley picking his nose “Most of them are Crows, keep picking up more and more of them in the In Betweens. ”  “Crows don 't, don 't exist. ”  Stanley snorted “Don 't they? Come on Rog, play the game, you can 't believe everything you see on TV. Lot of people in here that look like Crows, act like Crows, die hards talking the Raven is in the ascendancy bollocks. ”  “The Raven, Raven didn 't exist either. ”  “Going to be a difficult one you. ”  There was the Department of Convincing Cakes on floor six, a culinary operation investigating what happens when you blend highly potent mind bending drugs with deliciously baked goods. Sadly the budget had been cut after the obesity crisis, it was damned difficult to control a nations minds when they 'd all gone off icing. One sole baker was stirring mournfully at an old crockery mixing bowl when they walked in, vast arrays of mass production machinery lay unused behind him. He looked up hopefully as the men passed.

---

“Crack Forest Gateaux sirs? ”  “That would be, would be marvellous I haven 't eaten tod- ”  “Nope ” Stanley pushed the cake away “Steer clear of that one Rog, learned my lesson after the last batch of Smackaroons. ”  The Department of Definitely No Longer a Threat on four was off limits for now, they got as far as the ancient, ominously carved verdigris door to find a pale faced intern warning them that the moon was at the zenith of its arc and the Experimental Pulpos were having a particularly off day. Good to see, good to see the Peace Ministry still taking the Pulpo threat seriously, if one, if one knew the enemy and knew themselves, they need not fear the result of a hundred Spanish tentacles. All the departments had one thing in common, they seemed a little-  “Abandoneds a bit harsh, we 're just ticking along nice and lovely ” Stanley explained as they rode a glass fronted lift back down from the Department of Subconscious Whispers “Its just budgets and what the boss fancies, grief I 'd love a cigarette, he 's all in on Psychoacoustics now, have you got any cigarettes? ”  They exited the lift into the entrance hall.

---

The bottom floor did strange things to ones eyes, Rogers perceptions were dominated by a criss cross of black and white tiles surrounded by grubby, thin windowed, mostly wooden rooms. This was the floor spoken of in fearful tones, the one most abhorred by the denizens of the Peace Ministry, the Department of Meetings You Probably Don 't Need But You 're Having Anyway. For a workplace simultaneously housing two hundred terrorists and the unspeakable death god of g 'kakak there were a surprising amount of meetings about potential meetings to confirm meetings Down here was where they had the weekly procurement session, flour and ketamine don 't buy themselves. Off to one side the floor sloped down towards an immense vault door with a captains wheel style lock across it. “Whats down there? ” said Stanley. “I was just- ”  “Course you were, big interesting metal door like that. The Think Tank lives down there, gobbling up all your Govchats, pilotting all the drones, you name it, its in control of it. ”  “The permit system? ”  “No thats the Post Office. ”  “The military? ”  “After Tabuk? God no. ”  “Hospitals? ”  “Look just, anything techy you know what I mean?

---

Think of it as the I.T department, only its for the whole country and the computer knows more than the people ” Stanley caught sight of a rapid descent in moustache elevation “Don 't worry don 't worry, the boss is in control of it. No one gets in or out of there without a damn good reason. ”  Stanley buzzed signed them out with Kava at reception, Kava had just had a cheeky bit of PCPanettone and was having a lovely time. The two men stepped out into the cold and crossed the long stone drive, past a low row of bushes expertly trimmed in the shape of Tigers, Snakes and Dragons. The snakes were somewhat less impressive. A Silver Seraph sat idling beyond open wrought iron gates. “Nice to meet you Roger ” Stanley offered his left hand, Roger took it, an expert in shaking hands with either hand, as all men should be. “Absolutely, absolutely, raring to get myself involved ” his moustache bounced with anticipation.

---

“There we go thats the stuff ” he handed Roger a small square of plastic “Had to use your old picture from before you retired, sure you won 't mind. ”   Roger looked down in beatific silence at a version of himself he never thought he 'd get back, twenty years younger and even more fulsomely moustachioed. “Keep hold of that lad. You 're an Inquisitor now. ” Sit. Stare. Denunication. Two nights. Hunt for John Blard continues. Not thought to be dangerous, just questions. Would be in Mr Blards best interests to submit. Sit. Stare. Sit. Stare. Six more FWA arrested. Check back pocket. Still there. Thought to have links to Jones. Sent to Ministry of Peace for Inquisition. Sit. Stare  Sit. Stare. Buzzing. Buzzing outside. Smash of glass inside. Shit. The door creaked ever so slightly open. Bastard thing, of course it creaked, shouting to all the world here I am, wanted man and fugitive, and boy have I got some me for you to find. John had lost track of how long it was since he 'd last breathed, focused entirely on inching this noisy git open as slowly as he possibly could. He couldn 't help but feel he was making this unnecessarily dramatic. He stepped out into the chintzy hallway and peered down the stairs.

---

Nothing. Oh no, everything. The Drone hovered over the bar top, its spotlight glinting across the remnants of the optics. It was a sleek Five Eyes, these ones had guns, actual fire arms. Necess-   The Drone hammered into the door once, twice, then through it into the room, John threw up his hands and rolled underneath it out onto the stairs, down into The Big Deal, rolled across a table and stumbled headlong through the curtains to the Briefing Room. He 'd have taken a moment to pleased with himself had the Drone not buzzed back down the stairs with significant intent. “INTERLOPER. YOU ARE FLEEING A SOCIAL ORDER DRONE. SUBMIT YOURSELF FOR INSPECTION. ”  Shit. He retreated away from the curtain, searching for the second time this week, for an escape from this room. This was the worst pub he 'd ever been in, two sets of bastards and not a single packet of crisps. The window, the window might be a better shout this time.

---

It was a classic boozer bay window with white faded advertising stamped on the glass, the sort you can neither quite see in or out of, perfect for isolating you from the non-alcoholic world. “INTERLOPER. YOU HAVE TWENTY SECONDS. FAILURE TO COMPLY WILL RESULT IN IMMEDIATE TERMINATION. ”  John gave the window a gentle tap, it felt, well, glassy, but also pretty thin, like it wouldn 't stand up to a good hard chairing. He slunk back to the middle of the room and tried to lift the last remaining solid oak chair. Oh yes, very clever John, go for the massive wooden chair, the heaviest thing you 've lifted in your life is a bowl of soup and Mrs Leads baby. He scouted about the room, eyes settling on a broken off chair leg in the corner of the room. Perfect. “INTERLOPER. THE MARK FIVE SOCIAL ORDER DRONE IS FITTED WITH A SEMI AUTOMATIC AR15 RIFLE AND EIGHT HUNDRED HOLLOW POINT BULLETS. FOR YOUR SAFETY. ”  John raised the chair leg with trembling arms, holding it out like a baseball hitter practising his swing. One. Two.

---

He threw all of his weight behind the swing, putting all of his need for survival into that one swing, throwing every ounce of anger he had for Elleray Palm, concentrating it into the point of that chair leg, focusing that white hot rage into a single point of destruction. It bounced straight back off the window and hit him in the face. “INTERLOPER ” the Drone buzzed through the curtain rifle readied as John desperately checked he still had all his teeth and noses “YOU HAVE FAILED TO COMPLY, YOU WILL BE TERMINATED ” and then the windows exploded in a tempest of glass and wood as a body burst into the room. The massive form threw John to the floor as the Drone opened fire, shifting between the bullets towards it. They were huge in every way, dancing across the room with all the flexibility of a rhinoceros with an enthusiastic Ballet Instructor. They leapt and for one beautiful moment suspended in time, lit by the spotlight of the Drone, John saw Elleray Palms laughing face as he drove a knife into the very eye of the Drone. It dropped, to the floor, Palm following it driving the knife further and further until sparks flew from the stricken machine.

A leather waistcoat covered his back, groaning at the seams to contain his supreme mass, even at this distance the scent of koala bears was pungent. Tens of masked guards lined the perimeter, directing anyone that tried to head off down side streets back to the centre, pushing away those that didn 't understand the first time, flattening any who tried a second. Each of them was head to toe in black body armour, no discerning features but the way they held their guns. Many went for the “stay away from me else I 'll shoot you ”, the debonair mavericks of their caste carried it with a “Oh I have a gun, didn 't realise, maybe I 'll shoot you with it ” kind of air. Above the spectacle loomed Bigger Ben, not the Biggest Ben, but still a particularly large Ben. An Oohashi Node had been intertwined with it, a creeping ivy of wire and metal, pulsing out gentle, calming waves across the sea of pilgrims beneath it.

A hot air balloon tethered to it waved in the breeze, Esmerelda Jones face stretched out and bulbous on its inflated canvas. The top floor of the MoM, in blatant disregard for the Fire Safety Act 1987, was accessible only by a singular lift. A selection of registered users could enter using unique security cards, once inside the lift they would be scanned by a camera embedded in the ceiling that would analyse the biometric data of the entrant against a sample of their blood taken upon issue of the pass, down to their own individual balance of hormones, their scent, their very essence as a human being, technology so advanced it was found only in the halls of the governments most treasured crown jewel. Fortunately for a big faced man and his rapidly dwindling will to revolt, the camera had been switched off two days after it was installed because Big Dave Giblets kept forgetting his pass and no one could figure out how to override the bloody thing. Only its gone now, and you thought you could have it back, but it turned out you couldnt and the man who told you he 'd give it to you turned out to be a monster. Not even a present monster, he monstered you and then he left you to get monstered by an even weirder, creepier monster ” that was a lot of monsters but he was rolling now, you can 't let a word becoming a sound get in the way “You can 't hide down here in your holes pretending its nineteen fucking ninety five. Esmerelda Jones wasn 't a bad egg. She was the best egg. This is real.

---

They are stealing your people and blowing them up, and all you 're bothered about is Coronation Street and tamagochis for the kids. You have to do something. ”  “John, seriously John man ” Reza whispered again. “We have one shot before they brainwash us all. Right now, when they 're fighting in the Zones, normal average people raging at what they 've seen, while the Realists fight to put the genie back in the bottle.One chance to break Harmony and drop those buzzing wardens from the sky. Crawl out of your holes NIMBYs. You 're the only ones who can stop this. You can 't hide from life. Stop being so afraid and just fucking do something for fucks sake. ”  Silence. A smattering of applause that grew, spread, swirled in the air. A bubble burst, the crowd roared their approval, a cacophony of yeses that reached the very heights of the high domed ceiling, the ground rumbled with their stamping feet and clapping hands. The leaders of th Council listened in stunned silence. Reza elbowed John in the ribs.

---

“Ma- ”  “Reza I am fully aware of the irony in what I 've just said but I feel like this is a really key moment of realisation for me and I 'd appreciate it if you 'd keep your I told you sos until after I 've finished. ”  “Just saying man. ”  The members of the Inner Council disappeared into a huddle, muttering between themselves. Occasionally one would shake their head vigorously, the phrase “will of the people ” slithered its way out of someones arse and caused a stink. They motioned Maurice who was subsumed into the argument, violent Scottish murmurs just about audible. After a solid five minutes of mumbling observed by a crowd that had already made up its mind they broke. Cesira seized the initiative and stepped in front of John. “So. Will you stand with us ” the question hung in the air. “No. We 'll no stand with you ” Maurice denied her. He turned to todays rabbit in the headlights, John Blard “But we 'll stand with him. ” John had the sinking realisation that getting angry might have got him into trouble again. Maurice leapt on top of the table. “NIMBYs. Tonight, we drink, for tomorrow, we rise.

---

For too long we 've sat back and let that monster cripple this country, build an empire on the backs of our dead. Hidden in our holes for an easy life. Well no more. I hear you. These craven fuckers hear you. This man, The Walrus, he will lead us ” John shouted a vehement no but it was drowned out by the baying crowd “We 'll rise again. The phoenix from the flames. And when we 're done, we 'll stand in the fire, and we 'll say, no we 'll fucking scream, Not in my back yard! ” he screamed the last, foaming at the mouth, the whole crowd echoed him, erupting in tumultuous pandemonium, a crescendo of noise and stiff necked defiance that shook through to the surface. Cesira Brogue sat at a disappointing blue plastic table, alone, massaging her jaw and tapping her fingers to a beat that she couldn 't quite place. It was Mmmm Mmm Mmm Mmm by Crash Test Dummies, they 'd had it on in the tea room just down Corridor 5.

---

This damp corner of a storeroom was the best they 'd been able to find at short notice, the old briefing room she used to call an office had been converted into a nursery in her absence. The multicoloured elephants covering the walls were quite distasteful. Another in a long line of unsatisfactory work spaces. The door rattled as yet another gang of NIMBYs stomped past, music thumping out of one of their boom boxes. Under her regime everyone had had smart phones. Simpler times. The party had started the second Maurice Doris had bellowed his war cry, kegs of home brew beer appearing from nowhere and children disappearing to somewhere quiet. Much could be said of the NIMBYs approach to life, but they knew how to drink. Cesira had slipped away the second Oops Upside Your Head had boomed out from speakers that certainly hadn 't been there before, but not before Claire could punch her in the face. Just once. Her last vision of the revelries was a confused John Blard shaking hands with a queue of people and Reza Kaspersky trying to teach Ethel his dance moves. There was no place for her there.

---

In this quiet moment of reflection she had come to accept that it had been quite some time since she 'd known what people wanted. It was impossible to articulate that heady feeling of having a nation behind you, of being the one in power, the one whose responsibility it was to steer the lives of each and every member of this great country. Even harder to describe how it felt to lose it all to a man with no ability to lead, save for his rampant populism and penchant for telling people what they wanted to hear. No surprise he turned out to be a murderous tyrant, it was what the people said they wanted, after all. She noticed her fingers tapping and stopped them. That sort of lack of control was most unbecoming of a leader. But then, she was a leader no more. Deposed by a rebellion, forced to live with her enemies, then a man with no motivation but to go home had usurped her at every key moment. Reduced to obedience borne out of loyalty and, certainly in Jemima, pity. She 'd seen the look in her eyes as they botched a “State Address ” for the tenth time. Perhaps it was time to step back a little.

---

Butterflies of happy memories fluttered away in the wake of her doubts. Sometimes, it was difficult to know ones place in a story. John Blard couldn 't sleep. Not in a ghost of his best friend hovering over his shoulder accusing him of being complicit in her death sort of way, more a its been a busy day and he was struggling to shut off, sort of way. Nothing but embers remained of the party, it had been at least ten minutes since a drunk person had stumbled into the room, pissed in the corner and staggered back out. He wanted to hold a picture of his wife and look at it wistfully, think of happier times before things got terrifying tomorrow. But he really didn 't want to be a stereotype. Evan was snoring, lit by the dim light of Wozzys spotlight. Jemima sleeping through the snoring so close to him was a minor miracle. Ethel and Delta both dozed on cots in a darkened corner of the room, John hadn 't actually seen Delta asleep at any point in the time that he 'd known her. Every now and then he 'd catch her looking at him, plotting his demise. He stared at the ceiling and tried to process the evening.

---

Tomorrow they 'd get into a flotilla of vehicles and drive a convoy full of bombs directly at the Peace Ministry. He could still feel the arm gripped around his neck and see the demon in Maurice eyes. You don 't get hangovers, if you 're a NIMBY. Good to know Maurice had a plan, because he certainly didn 't. ---

I'm real sorry about that man, you don 't talk much about her. ”  “ It's OK. Its not a particularly great subject is it. At first he wasn 't sure about the blond but it suited her. ---

“Yeah and I 'm from fucking London ” Reza snorted “I get it man, you 'd be gone in a second if you could be. The Walrus ” he laughed so much the bed rocked. “Mate what am I going to do about that? Shit to do tomorrow innit. ”  “Night Reza. ”  “Night John. ”    The Ministry of Peace was an icicle drenched freeze frame of military precision, red coats lined the black marble stairs, those in guard towers saluted, Drones steadied their flight to witness the arrival of Vetko Block. ---

The door of the car opened slowly, a haze of cigarette smoke obscured the Prime Minister as stepped out onto the loose gravel of the courtyard. His grey suit had been slept in, his mustard shirt hung out of the back over his thin brown belt, his scrub of grey curls accentuated by his rough five o 'clock shadow. He flicked the butt of a cigarette up into the air and began his ascent up the stairs of the ministry. His eyes, unblinking and black focused squarely on the stricken form of Ian Baker, encapsulating him, imprisoning him, sucking him further and further into his orbit with every slow, calculated step, the man was frozen, his tongue darting out and eyes widening further the closer his predator came. He stopped mere inches from Baker and finally broke eye contact, looking up into the sky and taking a long inhale of the crisp cold air. When he looked back he was smiling, a smile that his eyes said he was lying about. “Hello Ian. This is a fuck up isn 't it. ” 15    A steady stream of elderly and children climbed onto a beige Erics Escapes coach idling at the entrance to the vehicle hangar.

---

Hangar was stretching the definition, it was more of an aspirational garage, big enough to fit the fifteen vehicles the NIMBYs had commandeered for what had been dubbed, to Cesiras infinite dismay, Operation Gang Aft A Gley. Or GAAG, for short. The last charge of the old and white brigade. There would be no subtlety, no sneaking through underground tunnels, mercifully few, if any, toilets. This was shock and awe, a convoy of pissed off NIMBYs surging out of PZ1 with one destination in mind. The Madhouse. A plan formed of sixteen pints in Maurice Doris, reliant entirely on overwhelming numbers and the unbeatable element of surprise. Cause as much aggro and shite as humanly possible, ya ken? Under cover of an absolute shitstorm get young Bogglehoffer to Harmony, turn that shite off, play that funky music and bobs your uncle. Or something, details on the escape had been in painful scarcity. “I could still just run away ” said John “I know it seems like we 're past that but I actually really could go over all that again. ”  “Whats it going to take for you to accept you 're not in Ohio anymore Toto ” said Reza.

---

“Its Kansas. ”  “Nah man ” Reza tapped his nose “Its Ohio, you know what I mean? ”  “I have absolutely no idea what you mean. ”  “Oh yeah man ” Reza nodded a smug smile Johns way “You know what I mean ” he winked. “Piss off Reza. ”  They wandered amidst an evacuation, a black and white show reel of brave speeches and lingering hugs with children that couldn 't understand why mummy and daddy were crying. The second this swarm of rust buckets rose from the underground this little haven would cease to be invisible. Maurice had made it clear to those that were willing to take part that the prospects of making it back were slim, he didn 't need to say that for most of those willing to stand up, their job was mostly to get in the way. Maurice had offered five of his best men to escort Evan into the heart of the asylum, but had been politely advised by both of Ethels knives that that would not be necessary. All the rest, the children, the infirm, those of nae use, were being piled onto two coaches to be whisked away to some other NIMBY bolt hole. They wouldn 't even have chance to stop at the Little Chef on the way.

---

The armada did not instil confidence. Two minibuses swelled full of rebels, the best one, the one with the plush chairs with arm rests on both sides had a little TV in the aisle. A Rover 850 speckled with auburn spots of rust had four lads hanging out the back of it smoking suspiciously fruity cigarettes. An Austin Montego had already broken down because they 're shit cars and thats what they do, an old Ford Escort sputtered away at the front. Bringing up the rear was a car shaped exactly like a hotdog, a relic of Minsters Cosy Hotdog Roadshow   Be careful, its a BANGER restored to its former, sausagey glory. The undead cars of the 90 's, dragged from their graves, hastily welded up with the thickest sheet metal in PZ1 and sent out to ride again; all lined up behind Maurice Doris pride and joy, a JCB Dozer with two exhausts taken directly from a space shuttle. They called it Behemoth, because he was a big Robot Wars fan. A woman in a hi vis waved the first coach out with those weird sticks the plane people have.

---

More than one parent broke down in tears as it disappeared from view, comforted by their comrades fortunate enough to be alone in the world. John joined the rabble waiting for weapons, Maurice Doris their Quartermaster and General. Reluctant though they might be, they knew how to mindlessly obey the results of a vote. The efficacy of the guns was questionable, they 'd been sat in a storeroom since the end of the Tumult, unused except for a couple of years ago when there were some rats with particularly scary teeth. Someone had dug out an old PA system and set it up above the booth, it was blasting out some Pet Shop Boys to get them all really pumped. ---

If this was the state of the guns John was feeling even less confident about the bombs stowed away in half the cars in the hangar, all rigged up to go off at the same time. All it 'd take was Delta Isol to slip on the detonator. But she wouldn 't. That was why she had the detonator. The former former soldiers turned soldiers cut a sad sight, piss and vinegar at best half full, protected by saucepan helmets and mothbitten body armour three sizes too small. The Tumtums went to war on the horse they rode in on, with fixed wheels and a bomb strapped to the inside of it.

---

The atmosphere in here was no more joyful. Jemima had her arms wrapped around Evan at the back of the bus, both of them quietly sobbing in the others embrace. Wozzy floated uncertainly over them, its camera chittering. “Tooled up? ” Delta gave them a curt nod. Reza laughed and shoved John forward. He showed Delta his weapon. Somewhere, in the back of a casino, forty thousand pounds in debt, half naked and afraid, Rod Hardys ears pricked up. She snorted. “Don 't get killed. People are counting on you. ”  “People keep saying that and I 'm not hugely clear on what for ” being a figurehead was already proving to be a pain in the arse. “Time to go Jem ” Delta called to her in a soft tone John hadn 't realised she had in her “Take Pete, no use to anyone. ”  There was a crash from the upstairs of the bus, followed by a bang and a couple of oofs. Pete flopped down the stairs and landed in an emotional heap.

---

He 'd progressed since John had last seen him, he was sporting a jet black wig with a sweeping fringe covering one of his eyes, the top of it sprang out in approximately fifteen directions, a tribute to the sun god found in the long lost Temple of Montemozuna. He had somehow got hold of a black t shirt with “Nobody knows how often I cry ” in bleeding white letters across the front of it, a belt made of bullets and had dark eye liner all over his face. “Why shouldn 't I go? ---

Reza slipped into the drivers seat as Jemima and Pete ran for the coach. Silence descended upon the bus, a moment of quiet introspection for some, an extra moment of working out if he could climb out of the window and leg it for John Blard. The ear splintering sound of an air raid siren filled the air. The clarion call. The Last March of the NIMBYs. The convoy boiled out of the earth, pissed off wasps going after the wanker setting fire to their nest. Behemoth led the way, incandescent orange flames belching from the immense exhausts as it roared through the streets. The flotilla burst out into the daylight and split off on alternating paths, spreading the chaos across the zone to converge on the vehicle checkpoints out of PZ1. Theres nothing less revolutionary than a traffic jam. Zoned out factory workers scattered in the face of the rushing onslaught, the queue for the supermarket was smashed like a pile of leaves in the wind as the hotdog van screeched around the car park, the smoking men screamed at the denizens of PZ1 to wake the fuck up, its happening.

---

From his viewpoint crammed into a corner near the stairs so as best to protect from, well, everything, John could see the faces of the zombified workers; glimmers of recognition on the faces of some, self preservation from the ones that scurried away from the horde of cars, only to come back together, gluing themselves back into the trusted patterns of normality. The convoy raced to the vehicle checkpoint. Drones across the Zone flittered ineffectually above the hordes, their weapons not readied for this unexpected uprising. Behemoth roared, louder now it accelerated away from the swarm, Maurice hung from the side of the cabin screaming bloody laughter as the enormous scoop battered into the mammoth sheet iron gate blocking their way. The Five Eyes guarding the checkpoint descended on Behemoth, firing shock rods and bullets into the bulletproof perspex surrounding Maurice. He didn 't flinch even as the plastic started to crack,the massive solid wheels of the thing lifted off the ground with the force of the impact but still Maurice didn 't let up, driving harder and harder, inching ever forward until. The gate bent outward, shards of metal from the mechanism holding it in place sparked across the sky, white hot with resistance.

---

Behemoth pushed and pushed until finally the shackles gave way and the solid iron gate burst outwards shaking the world as it fell. Over HAM radios and walkie talkies the NIMBYs celebrated, drowned out by the triumphant howling of Maurice Doris. The clamour of Behemoths engines filled the air once more, the flood seethed out of PZ1. Down here, next to the heart of Harmony the ringing wasn 't a ringing, it was singing, it was beautiful, it enraptured Roger and held him steady and made the complex lines of the world converge into sensible harmonious patterns. Solid patterns that drowned out the stuttering ghost that pooled in his feet and poisoned his thoughts. A sickening taint of rebellion. The Central Node was empty, technicians sent away at the arrival of the Prime Minister. He stalked between the terminals, hands trailing across empty desks and family photos. “I woke up today feeling utterly vivacious ” he enunciated every syllable with malicious glee, his gravel voice grating “ I thought, I 'll have a look outside, see how my mate Ian's handling things downstairs. What did I see Ian? ”  “Significant enhancements on the road to supreme control, Vetko ” Baker stood with his back arched, head tilted, his eyes following Vetkos pacing in an unmoving head, flicking left and right.

---

---

He used his arms to drag himself up the slope, hands closing around bleach white skulls, fingers slipping into eye sockets and behind jawbones, every inch earned with desperate energy. He could see her on the other side, keeping pace with every moment of the crawl. There was no land in sight, skull and bones stretching to the horizon in every direction, a landfill of death. The mountain was a pyramid, an enormous monolith that bent reality around it, blotting out all knowledge or sensation of anything other than the constant climb and the feeling of bone beneath his skin. He had to get to her. His breath came harder the higher he climbed, he could see her matching him step for step, he cringed at every slip that threatened to take her away from him. It was Erica, he knew that she was Erica and he knew that she was Jones. With every look there was a flicker, a metamorphosis of the two. She had her body and scent, he could hear the jangling of metal as she climbed and smell flowers and cigarettes. He knew that they were them and that it could be both of them and that he could love them both and that could mean whatever it needed to mean.

---

He had to get to her. After interminable wretched hours she reached the peak, staggering up onto a flattened platform before throwing herself across it even as he struggled, even as he fought to drag himself over the precipice. Ericas breath caught in a gasping choke in her throat. “I wanted it so bad ” she said, he could hear the rattle even as the words came in Jones ' voice. “Me too. ”   “Then I 'll come with you ” and she grasped his hands and John could feel every bone in her dying body once again, the horrifying feather light weight to her, she pulled him to her and he buried his face into her hair and he remembered that in the end it was soft and it was beautiful and it was her. The ground yawed beneath them. The mountain of skulls collapsed into itself, they fell, clinging together in the maelstrom of bone. And he realised she was dead. And then he woke up.
